Current Commentary

Resumption of Sino-Soviet Relations and the Ambiguity of the Current International Situation 18

(1) The Relationship Between China and the Soviet Union

The diplomatic relationship between our country and the Soviet Union was completely severed after the Sino-Soviet conflict over the Chinese Eastern Railway in July 1929. Although there were consulates stationed due to special local circumstances, these were only temporary measures taken out of expediency and could not be considered normal diplomatic relations. Later, Mr. Mo Dehui went to Moscow, but after repeated delays and negotiations, no results were achieved. The territories of China and the Soviet Union are connected, starting from Puli in Xinjiang in the west and reaching the gate of Jilin in the east, intertwined for over 10,000 li. In the world today, no other countries have such a close territorial connection. Although the areas where China and the Soviet Union border each other are not characterized by towering mountains and majestic rivers, but rather lie in remote and bitterly cold borderlands, which inevitably leads to geographical isolation, today, with the convenience of transportation by land, sea, and air, the barriers of mountains and rivers are as if they were next door. Although the political systems of China and the Soviet Union are different, and the ideologies they espouse are also different, the promotion of international circumstances and the need to safeguard peace in East Asia are sentiments shared by all countries in the world. The movement to resume Sino-Soviet relations was brewing in this atmosphere of peaceful foresight.

(2) The Triangular Relationship Between China, Japan, and the Soviet Union

When Japanese news agencies transmitted the news of the resumption of Sino-Soviet relations, this newspaper quickly published it, expressing its sincere hope for maintaining peace and welcoming the resumption of relations. If the unfortunate incident of July 1929 had not occurred between China and the Soviet Union, or if it had occurred and been resolved quickly, and normal diplomatic relations had been restored, then even if the Mukden Incident could not have been avoided, the ferocity of the Japanese warlords might have been slightly curbed. At the very least, the area along the Chinese Eastern Railway would not have been as devastated as it is today, and the territory within North Manchuria could have been preserved. The pursuit of justice and righteousness through the League of Nations would probably not have been entirely exploited by the Japanese, using fabricated cases to create ready-made facts.

In the current situation in Northeast China, economic power in the area of South Manchuria is entirely in the hands of Japan. In recent years, the construction of the Feng-Hai Railway and the Tao-Ang Railway, although not enough to compete with Japanese imperialism, the rise of national capital is an undeniable historical fact. This has aroused extreme jealousy from Japan, but the emerging forces are not yet fully developed and are difficult to contend with a powerful enemy in a short period. As for the Chinese Eastern Railway that runs through Jilin and Heilongjiang, it has been relegated to an ungoverned area by the Soviet Union, which is concentrating on its own development. This has allowed Japan to take advantage of the situation. The September 18th Incident has changed again and again, expanding and spreading to the three northeastern provinces. If it is not addressed, disaster will befall North China.

Fortunately, the League of Nations General Assembly has produced no results other than delay. The remarks of representative Yan Huiqing in Geneva were: "I am very pleased to represent China in restoring diplomatic relations with Russia. I have a feeling that the two major countries on the Pacific coast should restore normal relations for the sake of peace..." At the same time, the documents exchanged between Representative Yan Huiqing and Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov stated that "The governments of both countries are eager to promote friendship between the two countries for the sake of peace. Therefore, it has been decided that normal diplomatic and consular relations have been officially restored from today." We dare not say that the restoration of Sino-Soviet relations will solve the Far Eastern problem, and we dare not expect that the restoration of Sino-Soviet relations will bring some unexpected assistance. However, we know for sure that after the restoration of Sino-Soviet relations, there will be more convenience in general commerce, and politically and diplomatically, we will not be taken advantage of due to isolation. For the future of the Northeast, at least the enemy's convenience can be reduced.

(3) Changes in the Situation Between the United States and the Soviet Union

What we in our country should be concerned about regarding the resumption of Sino-Soviet relations, and what the international community should pay the most attention to, is the attitude of various countries towards China. Our country in the Northeast is already caught between two major powers and has nowhere to turn. In the mainland, it is even more surrounded by powerful countries and is more easily controlled. However, the situation in the Pacific is becoming increasingly tense, and relations between Japan and the United States are gradually worsening. For the sake of implementing its political strategy, the Japanese military clique is sparing no effort to work closely with the Soviet Union through Yosuke Matsuoka, hoping to gain deep understanding in order to counter the United States. At this time, the United International Press has submitted a proposal to the Senate Foreign Relations Committee to resume US-Soviet relations. It will still take time to realize, and although Japanese commerce may see a temporary decline, after the new President Roosevelt takes office, in order to solve the problem with Japan and for the sake of normal commerce, it will be inevitable to revisit the old issue. The restoration of US-Soviet diplomatic relations is also foreseeable.

(4) The Sudden Turn in Relations Between France and the Soviet Union

For fifteen years after the war, France and the Soviet Union have been preoccupied with "security guarantees." They have been concerned about the safety of Poland, fearing both the invasion of Germany and the spread of "red" ideology, so they have taken strict precautions and thorough safeguards. However, in recent years, this kind of hypothesis has been decreasing day by day. In order to maintain its advantage in Western Europe, France has no choice but to forge a distant alliance with the Soviet Union in order to reduce the assistance to the enemy and give its "security" a deeper guarantee. Furthermore, with the world economic recession, France needs a market, and the Soviet Union is the best and most promising investment market in Europe. Thus, France and the Soviet Union have progressed from normal diplomatic relations to signing a non-aggression treaty. During the tense period of the Northeast problem, the situation in Europe suddenly changed - France and the Soviet Union changed from enemies to friends. How could this be without a reason? The transformation of the world situation may change from sealed off to relatively open.

(5) Efforts Our Country Should Make

Our country is in this period of transition and must not fall behind again. Moreover, with a major enemy at hand, we must not lose the initiative. At this critical moment, our government has been able to overcome all difficulties and establish a unique diplomatic path, based on its own position, and restore diplomatic relations with the Soviet Union. This cannot be said to be not adapting to the times. Although it is inevitable to incur the enemy's jealousy, it is difficult to guarantee that they will not fabricate rumors to confuse international public opinion. However, for the establishment of peace in the Far East and for the struggle for national survival, we must move forward bravely, break the vile behavior of Japanese militarism, and promote human "justice and righteousness" with a spirit of dedication and sacrifice.

(Geneva) The Nineteen-Nation Special Committee held a closed meeting yesterday. British Foreign Secretary Simon continued to make remarks unfavorable to our country, advocating that the vague resolution of the League of Nations General Assembly on January 11 of this year be used as the basis for mediation, and not to use the facts in the Lytton Report that are unfavorable to Japan as the basis. (Central News Agency telegram, 13th)

Representative Yan Urges Special Committee to Publicize Report Within a Time Limit 19

Japan's Unchanging Stubborn Attitude Makes Mediation Hopeless

(Geneva) Dr. Yan sent a letter to the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee today, repeatedly requesting that the report be published on a regular basis in accordance with Article 15, Section 4 of the League of Nations Covenant, and declaring that the Chinese government had stated in the General Assembly on December 6 that it was prepared to accept the mediation method based on China's proposal, but if the Japanese government does not change the attitude expressed by Matsuoka, there is absolutely no hope for the success of the mediation process. Therefore, he hopes that the Special Committee will give due consideration to this key point when deciding on a certain deadline. The subcommittee drafting the proposal is scheduled to meet tomorrow afternoon. (Reuters, 12th)

(Geneva) Chinese representative Yan Huiqing submitted a memorandum a few days ago, firmly requesting the League of Nations to determine a definite date in accordance with Article 15, Section 4 of the Covenant, so as to publish the report on the Sino-Japanese dispute. The Nineteen-Nation Committee reviewed this memorandum when it met. The main points of its content are as follows: "My government is prepared to accept the mediation method in accordance with the designated basis. I have already declared this on December 6 at the Extraordinary General Assembly. However, the attitude of the Japanese government, as stated by its representative, is very stubborn. If this attitude is not changed, the hope of success of the mediation method is extremely slim." The Nineteen-Nation Committee has studied this mediation process and found it very difficult, because it cannot involve the content of the dispute and certain principles should be maintained. (Havas, 12th)

Chinese Representative Reports to the League of Nations on the Truth of the Yu Guan Conflict 20

(Geneva) The Chinese representative submitted two official documents to the League of Nations today, one regarding the Japanese army's shelling of Shanhaiguan on December 8. The Chinese representative stated that Japanese armored trains fired a total of ten shells, bombarding the town, and denied the Japanese claim that Chinese soldiers fired at the Japanese armored trains first. The other was a telegram from Song Ziwen, also about the Shanhaiguan incident, saying that Japanese civilians rushed into the customs office there and insulted the guards. (Reuters, 13th)

(Geneva) The Chinese delegation issued another declaration listing the various losses suffered by China since Shenyang was occupied on September 18. According to the statement, more than 58,000 Chinese people have been killed by Japanese soldiers to date, including 12,800 civilians, 25,000 volunteers, and 10,000 regular soldiers. (National News Agency, 12th)

The United States and Russia Participate in Mediation, Japan Still Expresses Opposition 21

(Tokyo) Reuters learned from responsible sources today that British Ambassador Sir Lindley had made friendly advice to the Japanese government on behalf of British Foreign Secretary Sir Simon, asking Japan to support the Geneva Mediation Committee, because this move seemed to be the only way to avoid the natural implementation of Article 15, Section 4 of the League of Nations Covenant in dealing with the Sino-Japanese dispute. Article 15, Section 4 "stipulates that if the dispute cannot be resolved in this way, the Executive Council shall, by a majority vote of all members, issue a report stating the facts of the dispute and the recommendations made by the Council that are fair and appropriate." Political circles here deny the report that British Foreign Secretary Simon threatened to propose the implementation of Article 4 of the Covenant if Japan refused to accept the Mediation Committee, and asked the Japanese government to express its deep appreciation for Simon's consistently friendly treatment of Japan. The Japanese government disregarded the advice of the British ambassador and telegraphed the Japanese representative in Geneva, ordering him to refuse to participate in the Mediation Committee organized by the League of Nations. This decision by the Japanese government is based on the reservations raised by Japan regarding the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee, believing that these reservations must also apply to the committee with the participation of US and Russian representatives. This committee is merely an expanded version of the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee. This instruction was issued after the cabinet meeting considered the matter. (Reuters, 13th)

The United States is Willing to Participate in the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee 22

(Geneva) US representative Davis told a reporter from the Central News Agency today that if the League of Nations itself finds it difficult to deal with the Sino-Japanese dispute and invites the United States to participate in the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee to discuss mediation methods, the US government will be happy to accept. (Central News Agency, 14th)

People's Hearts in Yu Guan Are Still Undecided 23

When the Bei-Ning Railway train arrives at the station, the pseudo-alert is even more intense. The Japanese army's Fifth Regiment Commander Gu Yi returned to Jin County in the twelfth year. Currently, there are more than 400 Japanese troops stationed in Yu Guan. There are still Japanese soldiers stationed at the station. The Japanese mothership and Asagao destroyer from Qinhuangdao withdrew to Yingkou and Lushun a few days ago. (Telegram, 13th)

(Beiping) About 500 righteous soldiers destroyed the railway at Shahuosuo yesterday morning, plotting to attack the pseudo-Fengshan train. Su Bingwen and His Entourage Can Arrive in Moscow Within Days, and Have Departed From Omsk Westbound. Su Gave a Speech to the Red Army in Irkutsk. 24

(Beiping) Su Bingwen's Secretary-General He Shengda telegraphed on the 11th, stating that Su Bingwen, Zhang Dianjiu, and 10 others, along with Mo Dehui's representative Wang Zengsi and Soviet Russian Foreign Affairs Committee representative Zimirilev, arrived in Irkutsk on the night of the 9th. All officers below Su are permitted to voluntarily return to China via Moscow to Europe. The Japanese newspaper said that they had been extradited, which is absolutely untrue. (13th)

Yu Xuezhong Talks About Tianjin's Public Security and Rumors of Japanese Recruiting Plainclothes Teams 25

Our army calmly responded and fought hard for nine hours. A Preparatory Meeting Will Be Held Today. The Major Mission of the General Assembly is to Resist Aggression and Save the Country. There Will Not Be Much Discussion on Local Party and Government Issues. 29

(Nanjing) The number of Central Committee members who have arrived in Beijing for the Third Plenary Session has exceeded the legal quorum. The focus of the discussion will be on dealing with the national crisis and deciding on major foreign policy issues. There will not be much discussion on local party and government issues. It is heard that the important cases of the Third Plenary Session are diplomacy and finance. The President of the Executive Yuan will not be changed and will still be held by Song. Nitre Has Been Recaptured, Wu Qiwai's Troops Have Reached Lichuan 38

Jiangxi Province Establishes Security Headquarters, Forming Five Regiments

(Nanchang) Wu Qiwai captured nitre on the 7th and advanced to the Fujian border of Lichuan. (Special dispatch from the 13th)

(Nanchang) Due to the spread of banditry, the Jiangxi provincial government is actively strengthening provincial defense, establishing a security headquarters, and forming five regiments. The first regiment is on the Jiangxi-Zhejiang border, under the command of the Sixth Administrative Region. The second regiment is stationed in the lower reaches of the Xin River, under the command of the Fifth Division. The third regiment is in Wuning, under the command of the Third Administrative Region. The fourth regiment is in the Qingjiang area. The fifth regiment has just been established in Pingxiang and is under the command of the Second Administrative Region. Each has considerable combat power. In the battles of Leping and Guixi, the first regiment defeated five regiments of Fang Shao's forces. They have wireless radios, telephones, repair shops, military hospitals, and other equipment. On the water, there are four ships: Xunyang, National Revival, and Liming. A lake defense headquarters has been established at Hukou, as well as a naval training center. Depending on the geographic and banditry situation, each county has mutual defense arrangements involving three to ten counties. (Special dispatch from the 13th)

(Nanchang) Chief of Staff Yu Hanmou and Lin Ying arrived in the province by plane on the 12th. (Special dispatch from the 13th)

(Nanchang) According to Ningdu refugees, the bandit puppet central government has established military, political, and party affairs training at the Yeshu Church north of the city. Every household has a cellar capable of sheltering a thousand people from aircraft. This year, able-bodied men have been drafted into the army three times. Men and women are registered and organized into teams. Every difficult task requires paying a tax of 400 cash, and even a child's bed must be taxed as property. Recently, the policy of killing people has been restored. Several hundred were brutally killed in the first half of the month. The head of the Huangzhu Lu regiment was first doused in kerosene and burned, then stabbed all over with knives. (Special dispatch from the 13th)

This order also states that Ye Huijun, a former member of the Tongmenghui, held righteous ideals and supported the Republic. During the Xinhai Revolution, he participated in military affairs with the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and made significant contributions. After the founding of the Republic of China, he did not boast of his achievements, remained true to his original aspirations despite hardships, engaged in business for many years, and was particularly enthusiastic about public welfare. Upon hearing of his sudden passing, we deeply mourn his loss. In addition to preserving his deeds for compiling the national history, a special commendation is hereby issued to recognize his legacy and to inspire future generations. This order.

The Southward Plan Has Been Changed to a Westward Invasion, South of the Great Wall to Inner Mongolia and Siberia

Philippine Independence Is No Longer in Danger 75

▲ National News Agency Washington, December 12th: Former US Envoy to China, Mr. Schurman, delivered a speech on the Philippine issue at the Catholic University here today, stating that Japan did indeed pay attention to southward expansion for a period of time, but since 1921, it has changed. Even during his tenure as envoy to China, he could perceive the actual change in its goals. Now it has definitely turned westward, even intending to expand south of the Great Wall of China to Inner Mongolia and eastern Siberia. Therefore, he believes that Japan will disregard the independence of the Philippines and adhere to its existing expansion plan, so there is no need to worry too much about the Philippines being seized by Japan after independence. The Philippine independence bill currently under review in the Senate, with a period of nearly 20 years, is too long. He believes that it should be granted freedom immediately.

British and French Parliaments Discuss War Debt Issues, Tomorrow's Payment Will Be the Final Batch 76

▲ National News Agency London, December 13th: Today, the British government replied to the United States, stating that Britain is prepared to pay the US war debt under the circumstances described in the previous note, showing that although the US government's attitude is firm, the British also hold the same determination. Today's British note stated that the British government must retain the right to raise these circumstances when considering the entire issue in the future. Regarding the US note's claim that the US President has no power to agree to change the predetermined payment terms, the British note stated that the British government did not mention any event that could affect the constitutional position of the United States. The previous note should only be regarded as specifically discussing the British government's own position, which was determined after careful consideration.

▲ Havas News Agency Paris, December 12th: The Chamber of Deputies held a meeting to discuss the war debt issue. First, Prime Minister Herriot made a declaration, followed by a reply from Member Maran. Then, the meeting was adjourned to allow Herriot to attend various committees. The Chamber is scheduled to reconvene at 3:00 PM tomorrow. When the Chamber was in session, hundreds of royalists opposed repaying the war debt and planned to demonstrate in front of the Chamber. Fortunately, the police had made arrangements in advance, and the security was very strict. The demonstrators were unable to approach the parliament, and several were arrested. The Chamber adjourned at 6:00 PM and is scheduled to continue the meeting the next day. Most of the police then withdrew.

▲ Havas News Agency Paris, December 12th: The Joint Finance and Foreign Affairs Committee of the Chamber of Deputies held a joint meeting at 7:00 PM, where Prime Minister Herriot and Finance Minister De Marcé discussed the recent negotiations between France and Britain regarding the war debt due on December 15th. Herriot stated that Washington had sent repeated communications, and then described the Anglo-French negotiations. This discussion took a very long time, and the committee was expected to adjourn very late. The meeting will continue at 2:00 PM tomorrow.

▲ Havas News Agency Paris, December 12th: At 3:30 PM, the Chamber began to discuss the war debt issue. The venue was packed. Prime Minister Herriot delivered a speech in an objective manner, first expressing respect for the United States' participation in the war. Then, he said that the misunderstanding between Europe and the United States was due to the United States neglecting European issues after the war, and Hoover's method of delaying war debt payments actually reopened the entire issue. France was most affected by the delayed payment because France suffered a loss of 1,650,000 pounds and lost its creditor status. In addition, France also allowed assistance to restore German credit. Although France endured such sacrifices, it did not receive any compensation, which is regrettable. Referring to the Treaty of Lausanne, Herriot said that this treaty more than doubled the credit of the United States and undoubtedly greatly benefited the United States. Herriot then emotionally said that France had fulfilled its obligations to the cause of international cooperation. He then explained how France negotiated with Britain and the United States, saying that Britain could have sought special treatment from the United States, but Britain did not, and its attitude was very honorable. Herriot continued that they are now seeking a solution with the least amount of harm. The methods of arbitration and outright refusal to pay are currently not feasible. For the sake of long-term interests and historical reputation, France cannot but respect the words it signed. The French people do not express opposition to the repayment of war debts. The government is not unaware of this, but in order to respect international promises, it must have a firm position. Moreover, France's counterpart has a US President and a US Senate, both of whom cannot make a final decision on the war debt issue. If France refuses to pay, what impact will it have? This must be considered in advance. As for Britain, it is especially important not to separate it from France.

▲ Reuters London, December 12th: Baldwin said in the House of Commons today in response to a request from the leader of the opposition party that the government has decided to dedicate Wednesday to the debate on the war debt issue. The speakers will be Chancellor Chamberlain, former Chancellor Churchill, former Chancellor Horne, Liberal Party leader George, Prime Minister MacDonald, and Labour Party leader Lansbury. Members who are dissatisfied with the attitude of the United States are expected to be very active in the debate. However, the government hopes that the discussion will not be intense. Any criticism of the government is naturally aimed at consolidating the government's rejection of future payments. It is generally said that the payment this Thursday will be the final batch.

▲ Reuters London, December 12th: Chancellor Chamberlain said in a speech in Whitehall today that we do not expect the proposal made to the United States to be accepted now, but we retain the right to raise this proposal when the discussion begins. At that time, if this proposal is handled with the friendly spirit that has always existed between the British and American governments, a satisfactory solution can be obtained. We have not demanded that our debtor countries pay their debts currently. He did not mean that the debts owed to the United States could be cancelled, but only that they could be delayed. If the countries that signed the Treaty of Lausanne cannot reach a satisfactory solution with the United States and find it impossible to ratify the Treaty of Lausanne, then we will restore the position before the Hoover moratorium, and we will still seek repayment from our debtor countries. How can the provincial government arbitrarily decide to abolish the department and limit the time for officials to leave their posts? Even if the provincial government wants to cut expenses, how can it come up with this idea? If it is said to be considering the burden on farmers, it should even more so move the donation for other uses. Moreover, China is founded on agriculture. Anyone with a little perspective knows that we are now striving for rapid progress, and are still worried about not being able to catch up with others. How can we bear to destroy the considerable foundation that has already been established by the provincial and county farms? In addition to telegraphing the central government to instruct the provincial government not to proceed with the previous decision, we respectfully ask all sectors to jointly uphold justice and prevent the destruction of industry. The Saito Cabinet, Beset by Difficulties and Disasters 83

Saito, who carries the banner of a cabinet uniting the entire country, was entrusted with the mission at a time of great difficulty, as a veteran of the Navy. The Army Ministry is harder than steel, constantly directing its affiliated right-wing groups to use intimidation at best and handguns at worst. The Seiyukai, which advocates constitutional politics, either agrees with the military or loudly sings the praises of constitutional normality. However, they all express extreme dissatisfaction with the current cabinet. Especially after the budget proposal was announced, although taxes were not increased according to the Army's wishes, the burden of 100 million yen in public debt placed on the people has also offended many capitalists. Takahashi Korekiyo, although a veteran of the Seiyukai, cannot suppress such grievances. Although the Minseito Party is willing to be a government party, it has too few seats and not much power. Therefore, at the beginning of the Saito Cabinet's establishment, some people estimated that its lifespan would be no more than three months or half a year.

Now it has been half a year, and it is always stabilizing in the midst of turmoil, achieving a temporary balance in the midst of competing factions. The 64th Diet will officially open on the 24th of this month, and the time is approaching. The attitude of each faction in the House of Representatives is indeed worthy of attention, and the antagonism between the members of each faction has intensified and become apparent from secret activities.

First of all, we see that the Seiyukai, which occupies 298 seats, has three cabinet members in the Saito Cabinet, but it is not satisfied with this. The self-respecting faction is very willing to assist the Saito Cabinet, but it also wants to express its own attitude. On the cabinet side, Takahashi and Mitsuchi have helped with finance and railways. On the diplomatic side, there is Matsuoka Yosuke's great activity in Geneva. Although they often express dissatisfaction with Saito, for the sake of the overall situation, they still believe that they should proceed in the direction of an emergency cabinet. At this time, they want to completely liquidate the relationship between the Saito Cabinet and the Seiyukai. To overthrow the Saito Cabinet is naturally not the time. However, the hardliners are very different. They believe that the Saito Cabinet wears the false mask of an emergency, calls itself a non-partisan, ultra-partyism, but is essentially a rebirth of the bureaucratic cabinet and an extremely ominous event in the history of Japanese constitutional politics. Letting this situation exist for one more day will hinder the development of constitutionalism for one more day, causing party politics to decline day by day. Moreover, the so-called emergency cabinet is to save the emergency period. Now that the budget to save the situation has been established, its mission has mostly been resolved. If it stays in power, it will indeed leave a very bad impression on future generations, leading the current politics to a point of no return. Therefore, it should quickly restore constitutional normality and organize a party cabinet. If the Saito Cabinet is reluctant to leave, the Seiyukai should publicly show its policies and announce its break with the Saito Cabinet based on a free standpoint. However, the fighting general of that faction, Mori Kaku, is currently ill and can hardly attend. Although there are still many people who express dissatisfaction, it is feared that it will be difficult to unify even within the Seiyukai. Therefore, in the parliamentary struggle, the situation within the Seiyukai party is also very worthy of attention.

The Minseito Party only has 122 seats. Even if Saito resigns, the government will not fall into the hands of the Minseito Party. This is something everyone knows. Therefore, the Minseito Party is oppressed by the Seiyukai and feels the fierceness of the military. To establish a political goal for itself, it has no power in fact. Therefore, it still hopes for the reappearance of an emergency cabinet. If an emergency cabinet is organized this time, it is generally observed in political circles that Ugaki Kazushige (the current Governor-General of Korea) will receive the great order. Therefore, the people of the Minseito Party are doing their best to establish a good relationship with Ugaki, preparing to occupy a more dominant position in the future than they do now. If the Seiyukai forms a cabinet, instead of hanging up the banner of a cooperative cabinet and only sending a few irrelevant cabinet members, it is better to let the Seiyukai form a single cabinet and restore constitutional normality, and the Minseito Party can prepare to rise again. Therefore, at this time, the Minseito Party is very willing to be a government party for the Saito Cabinet, and for the future Ugaki, it will adapt to the situation and create an opportunity to take the stage.

The Kokumin Domei, led by Adachi Kenzo, formally formed a party on November 22. It now maintains the position of a purely opposition party and has no special relationship with the current cabinet. Therefore, it maintains a critical attitude towards the budget for the next year, the policy of currency inflation, the disastrous drop in foreign exchange, the extreme anxiety of the people's lives, and the huge defects in finance. Although its claims have no chance of being implemented, its attack on the current government in the Diet will be quite fierce.

The total number of proletarian parties is three members of the Social Democratic Party, one member of the National Socialist Party, and one member who has left the Socialist Party and is still a proletarian. However, with only five seats, it has almost no status in the Diet. Its speech is just a speech, and its influence is very small. However, among the established parties, under the siege of capitalism and militarism, it also has a special value of existence. Although it cannot influence the Diet, it has a little fever-reducing effect on the crazy masses.

The lifespan of the Saito Cabinet and the future of parliamentary politics seem to be expressed in the 64th Diet. However, there are too many internal contradictions in the Seiyukai, and it is not easy to replace Saito. If Saito falls, the chaos may be even worse than it is now. At the very least, the successor must have a relationship with the military to be able to stand firm. (December 7, 1932, in Tokyo)

The Chaotic Situation in Sichuan 84

From a correspondent in Hankou: The Sichuan war has been going on for two months now, and the people have suffered greatly from the fighting, and the region has been destroyed. Although the central government has issued clear orders repeatedly, the Sichuan warlords have turned a deaf ear. Recently, Liu Wenhui withdrew from Chengdu, and Liu Xiang is still attacking Renyi. Observing the future, there is indeed a tendency for it to expand and prolong. Based on various circumstances, I record the general situation as follows:

Course of the Neijiang Conference 85

After Liu Xiang used his entire army and navy to capture Luzhou, Fushun, and Neijiang, the rich resources in the Zigong area became his sole possession. The generals of Deng Xihou, Tian Songyao, and Liu Wenhui's two units were brewing cooperation. Liu Cunhou and Yang Sen were also willing to join, jointly restrain Liu Xiang, and divide the land equally. Therefore, representatives from all parties gathered in Chengdu to discuss so-called ways to end the war. Liu Xiang knew that he was isolated, and secretly won over Deng, Tian, Liu, and Yang to maintain the name of the allied army, and convened the Neijiang Conference to oppose the Chengdu Conference. At that time, Deng and Tian were both in Chengdu. Deng had always defended Liu Wenhui, and was deeply dissatisfied because the telegram calling for a ceasefire had not been approved by Liu Xiang. Therefore, he ignored Liu Xiang's call for a conference. Tian had a secret agreement with Liu Xiang before the war, and sent Yu Anmin to Neijiang to assist in preparations. Yang Sen and Liu Cunhou had no preference between the two Lius, and sent representatives to participate in both conferences. Thus, the Neijiang Conference was held, and a resolution was passed to fundamentally eliminate the 24th Army. Liu Xiang's ambition to unify all of Sichuan grew even more as a result. Liu Xiang personally attended the conference, and was able to influence the attendees. The fickleness of the generals also contributed to this.

Liu and Tian Exchange Defenses in Chengdu 86

Two months ago, Liu Xiang and Tian Songyao agreed to solve the 24th Army together. The 21st Army was responsible for attacking the front, and the 29th Army was responsible for outflanking the rear. However, Tian Songyao was afraid to act rashly because Liu Wenhui's troops were strong. After Liu Xiang urged him, there was the first street battle in Chengdu. After the 21st Army ordered a general attack, Chengdu became quiet again. Furthermore, due to Deng Xihou's mediation, an understanding was reached with Liu Wenhui. Liu Xiang believed that since the war had already begun, it was impossible to back down. Therefore, he attacked Nei-Luzhou fiercely, and blamed Tian for breaking the agreement. Tian had long been thinking of stationing himself in Chengdu, and his heart was moved. Thus, the second fierce battle in Chengdu occurred. However, Tian's troops suffered great losses in this battle, and were forced to withdraw from Chengdu. Tian was extremely angry, and decided to cooperate with Liu Xiang. Liu Wenhui, facing enemies on both sides, had to ease one side. Therefore, he voluntarily withdrew from Chengdu on the 9th, allowing Tian to take over. Within a month, Liu and Tian alternately became the masters of Chengdu. Judging from the special situation in Sichuan Province, this is not surprising. However, it is said that during the fierce fighting, more than 10,000 people were killed, and property losses were countless, which is lamentable.

New Lineup of the Two Liu's Armies 87

With Tian's help, and because the Neijiang Conference decided to fundamentally eliminate the 24th Army, Liu Xiang increased his troops and attacked. He divided them into three routes. The central route was commanded by Wang Zuanxu, and departed from Rong County and Weiyuan, attacking Qingshen, Jingyan, and Renshou. Pan Wenhua and Tang Shizun's two divisions took the left route, along the Min River, attacking Jiading. Luo Zezhou and Li Jiayu's two divisions took the right route, along the Tuo River, attacking Ziyang and Jianyang. On the 9th, after receiving news that Liu Wenhui had abandoned Chengdu, he ordered a full-scale attack. The 24th Army also divided into three routes to meet the enemy. Renshou was the central route, Jiading was the southern route, and Liu Wenhui's main force was responsible for it. Zi-Jian was the northern route, and Deng Xihou's troops were responsible for it. All sides have already made contact, and the outcome has not yet been determined. According to a telegram from Sichuan Province from a certain gentleman from Sichuan, Liu Xiang's side seems to have the upper hand, and Liu Wenhui's troops have been defeated again. However, the strength of the 24th Army is still sufficient, and its base is also wide. It is not easy to fundamentally eliminate it.

Liu Wenhui's New Plan 88

Liu Wenhui, holding the title of chairman, was by no means willing to give up Chengdu. Because the Yu and Tian armies attacked from both sides, it was difficult to cope with. Therefore, he had to reluctantly give up Chengdu in order to appease Tian's army, so as to concentrate on resisting Yu's army. The troops originally stationed in Chengdu have now withdrawn to Xinjin, 120 miles from the city, and built fortifications to prevent Tian's army from advancing. The central route is stationed in Renshou, the southern route is stationed in Jiading, and it is closely connected with Deng's troops stationed in Zi-Jian to resist desperately. Liu also has a new plan. If Zi-Jian and Renshou cannot be defended, then they will be abandoned together, concentrating on Qingshen, Meishan, and the Ya'an area to shorten the defensive line and preserve strength. Then, taking advantage of Yu's army's exhaustion, he will launch a counterattack again. In case the situation changes again, he will implement the plan to develop the Kang region, and reorganize his troops. The situation in Sichuan is complex. The so-called allied army front will soon merge due to the uneven distribution of spoils. This is also the time for Liu Wenhui to rise again. Therefore, he would rather give up a thousand miles of land to others than to use a single soldier or a single gun to help the enemy, which can also give a glimpse into his intentions.

In summary, the current war is fierce, and there are many hidden dangers in the future. If the situation in Sichuan is not reformed in time and allowed to compete for hegemony, the people of Sichuan after the catastrophe will never have time to recuperate. (December 12)

A Record of Inspecting the Recovered Areas After Suppressing the Communists (1) 89

The country is in turmoil, and internal and external troubles are coming one after another. The central government believes that it is necessary to settle domestic affairs before resisting foreign aggression, and has specially established the General Headquarters for Suppressing Bandits in the three provinces of Henan, Anhui, and Hubei, with the headquarters in Hankou. Generalissimo Chiang Kai-shek, member of the Military Commission, concurrently serves as the commander-in-chief, stationed in Hanyang, overseeing the army, and focusing all efforts on suppressing the communist bandits in the three provinces of Henan, Anhui, and Hubei. In the past six months, great achievements have been made. The major communist bandits such as Xu Xiangqian, He Long, and Kong Hechong have been successively defeated, and their nests have been leveled. There are not many remaining bandits, and they are scattered and fleeing. A major campaign is currently underway to completely eliminate them and recover dozens of bandit areas. After the great catastrophe, the fields are desolate for thousands of miles, and the residents are gradually gathering but have nothing to live on. The key to good follow-up work lies in collective wisdom and effort. Generalissimo Chiang Kai-shek, in view of this, invited civic groups from various provinces to organize an inspection group to personally inspect the recovered areas in order to combine the power of the entire country and seek a quick recovery. Groups from Beiping, Shanghai, Nanjing, and other places successively organized and gathered in Hankou to set off together. The Beiping City Inspection Group arrived in Hankou on the 30th of last month, and the reporter also joined its ranks. On the evening of the 28th, I left Beiping by train to the south. The situation along the way is as follows: From Ping to Zheng, the road is peaceful, and the residents are bustling and lively, with a sense of peace. South of Xuchang, vigilance is gradually seen. From Jigongshan and Wushengguan to the Guangshui area, the ridges and peaks along the road rise and fall, and the terrain is dangerous. Even in the daytime, the garrison is still scattered on the ridges on both sides, with sentries to guard against unforeseen events. The vigilance at night is even more evident. According to the personnel on the road, although the major communist bandits have been defeated, the remaining bandits are scattered and still being wiped out. The garrison's day and night vigilance, daring not to slack off in the slightest, is to prepare for any eventuality. From Guangshui to Hankou, all the stations passed have anti-communist slogans, which shows that the authorities are focusing all their efforts on this, and will not stop until the goal of complete elimination is achieved. Suppressing the communists is a fundamental national issue. This inspection of the recovered areas is different from ordinary inspections. We must observe from the perspectives of military, politics, economy, society, and people's livelihood in order to be thorough. The reporter is not talented, but I am willing to investigate based on this purpose.

The Course of Suppressing the Communists in the Central Hubei Area 90

After last year's flood, the people along the river in the Central District were ruined and unable to make a living. Many were willing to take risks and were incited by the communist bandits. The central government was also too busy with disaster relief to handle the suppression. Therefore, the bandit forces gradually increased. The bandits used the flood to coerce the people to flee north and seek food in the highlands. After the flood receded, they gradually moved east, planning to cross the Pinghan Railway and join forces with the Xu bandits in the East District to occupy Wuhan as a base. At that time, the garrison in Hubei Province was weak and had no overall plan for suppressing the communists. They suppressed in the east and defended in the west, unable to concentrate on suppressing the bandits. As a result, the clowns jumped around and became unmanageable. This spring, Xu Yuanquan, commander of the 10th Army, led his troops to suppress the bandits, concentrating on Yingcheng and advancing westward. At that time, the communist bandits in the Central District were He Long's fake 7th Division, Duan Dechang's fake 8th Division, and Wang Yimin's fake 9th Division. Most of them were concentrated in northern Hubei. After the government army recovered Huangshi, it divided into two routes to suppress the bandits. One route was led by Hua Wenxuan, leading a part of the 49th Division to advance west. The other route was led by Zhang Zhenhan, transferring a part of the 41st and 48th Divisions to advance. Hua's troops advanced to Wamiaoji and were surrounded by bandits. Zhang's troops were also trapped in Daijiahe City. The Red Army and militia surrounding the two troops numbered about 100,000, and the situation was extremely tense. The rear urgently dispatched reinforcements from Zaoshi to rescue them. In the Baimamiao area, they confronted the bandits for a month. Later, Hua and Zhang's two troops bravely broke through the encirclement and joined forces with the Baimamiao reinforcements, defeating the communist bandits. In this battle, the communist bandits spent a lot of bullets and suffered extremely heavy casualties. He Long and Wang Yimin led the remnants to flee back to Honghu, while Duan Dechang fled west. The government army split up to pursue the bandits. One route tracked south from Laoxinkou, another route attacked Fengkou from Mianyang, and another route advanced west from Qianjiang. They engaged in fierce battles with the bandits in Laoxinkou, Xingouji, and Yanglinguan. The 41st Division, which pursued the communist bandits on the northern route, occupied Laoxinkou. The bandits fled from Xingouji to Yanglinguan, and encountered the government army. They were hit head-on and fled back to Xingouji. At that time, Xingouji had already been occupied by the 41st Division, but the bandits did not know, and were surrounded. Most of them were disarmed. The communist bandits' important political workers Lu, Xia Xi, and Ma Wu were all captured. The bandit forces then fell into a slump. He Tu led the remnants to flee west, and the old nest of Honghu was taken like a bamboo splitting. The suppression of bandits in the Central District came to an end.

Inspection of Yingcheng, Changjiangbu 91

Our reporter traveled with the inspection team on the 7th, departing from Hankou by car. The Central China District Headquarters dispatched Councilor Wang Yiqun, Adjutant Han Mutao, and Tenth Army Chief of Staff Yang Shaodong to assist along the way. They set off at 9:45 AM, heading northwest along the Chuanhan Railway base. The Chuanhan Railway was the fuse that ignited the Xinhai Revolution. The Qing Dynasty borrowed British funds to build over 200 li of railway base. Construction was halted after the change of era, and now only ruins remain. Ten li from Hankou, a German-style fort stands. The fort is circular, about thirty feet high, divided into four or five levels, with cannons mounted around it for all-round firing. Trenches were dug in front, and electric fences were installed, with soldiers stationed for defense. This was because during the rampant activities of the communists, there were rumors of attacks on Hankou, causing great alarm, with several scares in one night. The fort was built for defense against any eventuality. At the 40 li mark, in the Maoerhe area, the bridge was destroyed by the communists in November last year and has not yet been repaired. From there west to Yingcheng, all bridges passed were burned, demonstrating the extent of communist activity. The Central China District communists used Caohu as their base in the east, and then moved eastward, sending plainclothes teams to disrupt transportation to prevent government troops from suppressing them. The communist strategy for ravaging the region was to divide it into "red zones" and "gray zones." In the red zones, the communists implemented communism, treating it as occupied territory. The gray zones were unoccupied areas, where they conducted harassment, sabotage, and intimidation before eventually occupying them and turning them into red zones. Previously, the area west of Xin'andu and east of Yingcheng was considered a gray zone by the communists and was constantly harassed. At 10:45 AM, the car arrived at Xin'andu. In January of this year, the bridge there was burned by the communists, and the village was looted twice. Around 1:00 PM, they reached Manjiagang and Maijiahe, where the three counties of Yunmeng, Xiaogan, and Yingcheng meet. This place is about 100 li from Hankou, and the communists had been there several times, only looting and leaving without occupying it for long. They then arrived at Changjiangbu, a large rural town that had been attacked several times by the communists and suffered some damage. Residents are now gradually returning. At 3:00 PM, they arrived in Yingcheng for inspection. Yingcheng is the center for suppressing communists in Central China and is very important. It was attacked by the communists two or three times but was not captured due to the resolute defense of the garrison and local militia. In February of this year, a large force advanced to suppress the communists, concentrating on Yingcheng and first clearing the communist nest in Caohu. In April, the communists were defeated, and their base in Caohu was captured. The communists near Yingcheng were then cleared. The city of Yingcheng is still in good condition, as it was not devastated by the communists. However, the surrounding rural areas suffered terribly from the communist ravages. The local authorities are now working hard to revitalize the area, establishing a Post-War Relief Committee to plan everything. For self-defense, there is a Security Team reorganized from the militia and a Communist Suppression Volunteer Army. The Security Team has about 800 men throughout the county, and the Volunteer Army is organized by able-bodied men from various villages. The county has convenient transportation, with telephone and telegraph, making it easy to assemble the Security Team and Volunteer Army. (Reported from Yingcheng on December 7th)

The Liu Army in Laiye Has Fully Withdrawn, Provincial Committee and County Magistrate Enter the City to Conduct Official Business, Shandong Province's Civil Administration Is Now Unified 92

Jinan Dispatch: The Jiaodong Incident has been resolved. Liu Zhennian's troops are being transferred to Zhejiang and Fujian. The Second Brigade stationed in Laiyang was the first to depart, followed by the direct subordinate units of the division. The First Brigade will also depart soon, all overseen by Deputy Division Commander He Yisan in Yantai for boarding ships. The Liu troops in Laiyang completed their withdrawal on the 6th. On the 7th, Provincial Committee and County Magistrate Yang Yougui entered the city from Shuigoutou to take over. Laizhou is a bit farther from Yantai, and its base, so the withdrawal was delayed. Today, news from Laizhou indicates that the Independent Brigade of Zhang Luanji's troops stationed in Laizhou began heading to Yantai on the 8th. By the 9th, they had completely withdrawn from Laizhou. After receiving the report, County Magistrate Zhao Hongze immediately sent forty members of the United Village Association from Shahe at noon to clean up the city first. Zhao led the county government and various bureau personnel from Shahe into the city at 8:00 AM on the 10th. Because the local losses after the war were severe, they are now working on post-disaster relief. They also telegraphed the provincial government to report. Since the sudden outbreak of the Jiaodong Incident, Laizhou was occupied by Liu Zhennian, and the county government moved to Shahe for three months. Now that the Liu army has withdrawn, they have finally been able to return to the county seat, and provincial administration has been unified. (December 11th)

Page 9

Thoughts of Chinese and Russian Figures on the Resumption of Diplomatic Relations

Wu Chao-chu Talks About Good International Influence, Laiwen Talks About Important Commercial Relationships 104

Chinese envoy Wu Chao-chu is scheduled to go to Beijing today from Shanghai to attend the Third Plenary Session of the Central Committee. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mr. Wu at his residence yesterday and asked for his opinion on the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia and the content of the proposals for the plenary session. He kindly received the reporter and gave a detailed answer as follows:

Resumption of Diplomatic Relations Between China and Russia 105

According to Mr. Wu, the United Kingdom, France, and other countries have long had diplomatic relations with Soviet Russia. The movement for the resumption of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia is also actively underway recently. Diplomatic relations between China and Russia have been severed since 1927, more than five years ago. The resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia is indeed a beneficial thing that should be done at present. Now, the governments of China and Russia have announced that, to enhance friendly relations between the two countries, they will formally resume normal diplomatic and consular relations from yesterday (that is, the day before yesterday). This move will have a good impact internationally. However, the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia will have a minor impact on the Sino-Japanese problem, but it is feared that there will be no major changes. Whether Soviet Russia can assist our country in solving the Northeast problem, of course, we cannot predict it before Soviet Russia has clearly expressed its views. However, the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia is a beneficial thing that should be done, and this is indeed an unquestionable and definite fact.

The Sino-Japanese Problem 106

The League of Nations has now handed the Sino-Japanese problem over to the Special Committee of Nineteen Nations to discuss solutions. The Sino-Japanese problem cannot be resolved by the League of Nations Executive Council, nor can it be resolved by the League of Nations General Assembly. Whether the Special Committee of Nineteen Nations can produce a satisfactory solution is indeed a worrying question. In my personal observation, the Special Committee of Nineteen Nations may also find it difficult to produce a successful solution to the Sino-Japanese problem. However, the United States recently stated that if the position of the League of Nations differs from that of the United States, the US government will refuse to participate in the Special Committee of Nineteen Nations. This statement is tantamount to a warning to the League of Nations, and this warning may make the work of the Special Committee of Nineteen Nations smoother. In short, if we rely solely on others for the Northeast problem, it will be difficult to obtain good results. The Chinese people must use their own strength to plan for solving the Northeast problem. The Volunteer Army is now fighting hard against the enemy in the Northeast, exerting its own strength and actively proceeding to recover lost territory. It is deeply hoped that compatriots throughout the country will enthusiastically assist the front line, and do not allow the Volunteer Army in the Northeast to be like General Su Bingwen's exhaustion of ammunition and supplies, leaving the country in tears. I am scheduled to go to Beijing tomorrow (that is, today) to attend the Third Plenary Session of the Central Committee, and I have prepared four proposals: 1. the Sino-Japanese problem, 2. disarmament, 3. industrial development, and 4. the establishment of popular opinion organs. The above four proposals have now been drafted and will be submitted to the plenary session for discussion. As for the content, it must wait until it is registered by the secretariat of the plenary session before it can be officially announced. At the moment, it cannot be published. Mr. Sun Zhesheng is scheduled to go to Beijing tonight (that is, last night) first.

Russian Expatriates Are Gratified 107

A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency visited Mr. Laiwen, the Shanghai commercial representative of Soviet Russia, yesterday and asked about the attitude of Russian expatriates after the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia. According to the conversation, the Russian side is even more delighted about this. The Russian side is even more pleased about this. It believes that China and the Soviet Union not only have important diplomatic relations, but also very important commercial relations. From now on, expatriates from both countries can also mutually enjoy the convenience of the resumption of diplomatic relations. It is hoped that the people of China and the Soviet Union will continue to work hard to move forward. The former Soviet Russian Consulate in front of the Waibaidu Bridge, which is currently being held in trust by him, may soon be restored. Another Russian then asked the reporter about the attitude of the Shanghai press towards this matter. The reporter replied that the issue of the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and the Soviet Union has been introduced by the press, and now that it has been realized, everyone is of course happy. Finally, the reporter asked whether there was news that Su Bingwen's family members and others had come to Shanghai from Vladivostok. Laiwen replied that he had not received a telegram.

The Remaining Two Million Yuan of Shanghai's Revival Public Bonds Will Be Sold Tomorrow 109

▲The British Firm Lyen Line Entrusts HSBC to Sell on Its Behalf

The Shanghai Municipal Government is issuing six million yuan of Revival Public Bonds for the revival of the war zone, using the income from dockage fees as collateral. Now, the regulations and draft agreement have been approved by the Executive Yuan one after another. Four million has already been underwritten by the British firm Lyen Line, and the remaining two million yuan of public bonds are scheduled to be sold by HSBC on behalf of the firm tomorrow (the 15th). The information obtained yesterday is recorded as follows:

Issuance Method 110

These six million yuan of Revival Public Bonds are entirely for the revival of post-war municipal undertakings. The interest rate is seven percent per week, and there will be two lotteries. The municipal government will use the income from dockage fees in the city as funds for repayment of principal and interest. The face value is set at 1,000 yuan and 100 yuan denominations, which can be freely mortgaged and sold, and can also be used as guarantee deposits, collateral, or foundation reserve funds for public affairs in Shanghai or public organizations. The six million yuan of public bonds are all underwritten by the British firm Lyen Line.

Director Cai's Conversation 111

Yesterday, the reporter interviewed Cai Zengji, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau, to inquire about the method by which Lyen Line is underwriting the Revival Public Bonds. According to the conversation, the temporary contract has been approved by the Executive Yuan and sent to the municipal government. As for Lyen Line, the other party underwriting, the time for [blank space] decision is when the temporary contract is formally approved by the Executive Yuan and sent to Shanghai, and after the other party has reviewed the approval and found it to be correct, it will be effective. Therefore, there is no need to handle a formal contract or signing procedures separately. The draft agreement will serve as the formal contract. The total amount of public bonds is six million yuan. Except for the four million underwritten by Lyen Line, the remaining two million will be dispersed outside, so it is now scheduled to be sold by HSBC tomorrow (the 15th) from 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM in the morning and from 1:00 PM to 1:00 PM in the afternoon. The first installment of the funds has not yet been paid to the municipal government. It will probably not be long before it is paid.

Reviewing the Approval 112

After the Executive Yuan's approval of Shanghai's issuance of six million yuan of Revival Public Bonds arrived in Shanghai yesterday, at 11:00 AM, Westerners from the British firm Lyen Line and HSBC each went to the Fenglin Bridge Municipal Government to review the original approval as a basis for it to take effect. Cai Zengji, Director of the Finance Bureau, accompanied and received them, and met with Secretary-General Yu to read it. Both parties were satisfied and dispersed at noon. Later, the reporter learned from other sources that the city's dockage fee income was about 700,000 yuan last year, with about 150,000 yuan receivable each quarter. This fund will now be used as the fund for repayment of principal and interest on the public bonds. (Guo Wen She)

Datong Company's Hongda Steamer Was Seized 119

A telegram was received last night asking to send a steamer to tow it to Shanghai

The Company Telephoned Urgently to Inquire 120

The Hongda steamer left Shanghai at 2:00 AM yesterday (the 13th), loaded with goods and passengers to be exported to various ports such as Tongzhou and Yangzhou. The company suddenly received a report yesterday afternoon stating that the Hongda steamer was seized by pirates, but the details were unknown. At that time, the Zhida steamer happened to be returning to Shanghai from Yangzhou. The company immediately asked the crew of the steamer if they had seen Hongda on the way. Passengers and Goods Carried on the Steamer 121

Afternoon, Still No News 122

We can only wait for definite news before discussing further measures. It is rumored that the incident occurred outside the Wusongkou, and the pirates took the people and the ship to Daquyang. It is also possible that we will have detailed news today.

Telegram Reporting Robbery 123

Yesterday at 4:30 PM, Datong Company received a telegram from a small island at the mouth of the Yangtze River stating that when the Hongda ship was leaving the port, it was attacked by nine pirates, each armed with weapons, who boarded the ship and robbed for several hours, damaging the machinery severely, resulting in substantial losses. The ship is now docked near a small island, requesting immediate towing back to Shanghai for repairs, etc.

Nantong Telegram Not Received 124

A telegram from Nantong on the 13th stated that the Shanghai-Yangtze River route's Hongda ship had not arrived in Nantong on the 13th, and its whereabouts were unknown.

The Station Was in Complete Turmoil All Day Yesterday 125

Villagers in Pengpu District Attempted to Petition in Beijing, Requesting Vehicle Allocation, but the Railway Bureau Did Not Approve It. The Situation Was Resolved After Mediation by the Director of the Cultural Affairs Bureau. 126

Villagers in the Pengpu District had previously petitioned the Railway Department repeatedly regarding the construction of a new site for the railway, requesting consideration of the people's hardships and a reduction in the land acquisition, but to no avail. They then agreed to go to the North Station yesterday morning with all the farmers to take a train to Beijing to petition. A total of seven hundred men, women, and children gathered and set off. However, the two railway authorities, seeing too many people, stopped them, which led to a conflict. As a result, forty people still took the train to Beijing. The details are recorded below:

Departure Situation 127

Yesterday morning, while it was still dark, villagers from the entire Pengpu District, carrying the old and supporting the young, gathered in the town. At that time, the crowd was dense, about seven hundred people. The villagers elected Hou Xuanqing, Tao Wenyuan, Zhao Youting, Zhang Zhongxiang, Zhao Wenxiu, Hou Shizhang, and six others as representatives, and ten inspectors to lead the way to the North Station. They arrived at the North Railway Station at eight o'clock. Each villager wore a cloth badge identifying them as Pengpu Petitioning Villagers and carried petition flags, dispersing inside and outside the station.

Requesting Vehicle Allocation 128

After arriving at the station, the representatives, led by Hou Xuanqing, contacted the railway authorities to negotiate for vehicles. Because this petition concerned petitioning the Railway Department in Beijing, Fan Zhaolan, the special commissioner of the two railway police departments, Lin Zengding, the police chief, and many inspectors from the Public Security Bureau, due to the large number of petitioning victims, found it inconvenient and politely refused, but the villagers did not agree and insisted on taking a train to Beijing.

Dispute Arises 129

At twelve o'clock, there was still no result. The villagers wanted to take a train to Beijing at 12:15. As the train was about to depart, they crowded into the station and tried to board the train automatically. Zhang Yingxin, the ticket collector at the platform, stopped them, which led to a conflict with two elderly women among the villagers, Tan Li (64 years old) and Tao Zhu (43 years old). Seeing this, the villagers were very upset and came forward to negotiate with Zhang, tearing off his clothes buttons. Later, the police department summoned Zhang to the department, and the matter was resolved.

Delaying Train Departure 130

After this incident, many villagers crossed the platform to the tracks to prevent the 12:45 express train from departing. At that time, the Public Security Bureau sent additional inspectors to mediate, and Commissioner Fan also agreed to allow the six representatives to take the train to Beijing for free. The representatives of the villagers then persuaded the villagers not to stand on the tracks and to wait for the train to depart. The express train was able to depart, but it was delayed until 1:30.

Discussing Numbers 131

Later, the representatives of the villagers negotiated with the Railway Bureau again. The Railway Bureau only allowed six people to travel free of charge. If everyone went to Beijing, they had to buy tickets to sit down, but the villagers did not agree and were willing to send sixty people to Beijing for free, and the rest would return home.

Preventing Vehicles Again 132

Police Chief Lin Zenghua and Police Commissioner Fan Zhaolan continued to negotiate with the representatives of the villagers. The villagers firmly demanded that one hundred people go to Beijing. It was already three o'clock, and the second express train was about to depart at three o'clock. In order to prevent another train obstruction incident, Lin and others agreed to negotiate with the Railway Bureau, but after the negotiation, Lin and others replied that the Railway Bureau had no solution. The villagers were very angry. At this time, it was discovered that the Shanghai-Changzhou train at four o'clock was also about to depart, so they rushed to the platform and stopped the four o'clock train.

Firing Trend 133

At this time, a railway policeman on the platform suddenly fired a gun into the air as a warning. Fortunately, the bullets went upwards and did not injure anyone. A railway policeman firefighter also took a leather dragon head and sprayed water on the villagers. The villagers were even more motivated and dragged the firefighter out, forcibly tearing off his uniform symbols before releasing him to vent their anger. A large number of people still rushed to the platform to block the front of the train, not allowing it to depart. The train had to be temporarily suspended.

Special Martial Law 134

At this time, the Public Security Bureau received the news and immediately sent seven or eighty policemen from the Fifth District, along with more than three hundred security guards, to surround the station. Only exiting the station was allowed, and entering the station was prohibited. At the same time, a patrol car from the Concession arrived and stopped in front of Laifenglou on the border road. Fifty or sixty Chinese and foreign patrolmen temporarily imposed martial law. Passengers from Shanghai-Hangzhou and Beijing-Shanghai were not allowed to leave their houses if they lingered on the border road. More than two thousand passengers arriving in Shanghai were temporarily blocked at the station, unable to cross the line.

Wen's Mediation 135

The Police Department saw the tense situation and reported it to the Director of the Public Security Bureau, Wen Hongen, asking him to come and mediate as soon as possible. Wen arrived in a car with his entourage at five o'clock in the afternoon and explained to the representatives of the villagers and verbally agreed on two conditions: ㈠ The Railway Bureau would issue a free round-trip ticket (which would allow ten people to ride). ㈡ Seven representatives from the villagers would persuade the villagers to explain the difficulties of taking the train. The seven representatives agreed to proceed, and sent Zhao Wenxiu and Hou Xuanqing to explain to the villagers. As a result, they were satisfied but stated that if the petition in Beijing was unsuccessful, they would still take the train to Beijing as a whole. A storm was resolved, and it was already 7:30. The Shanghai-Changzhou train, which had been scheduled for four o'clock, departed at 7:30.

Result: Going to Beijing 136

Last night, after Wen Hongen mediated, the villagers were dismissed by the representatives and ordered to return home, but thirty men remained. The thirty men bought tickets and went to Beijing with the ten people, making a total of forty people going to Beijing.

Page 10

They first went to the Dachunghua News Agency to find food, and at ten o'clock, they took the train to Beijing, planning to first petition the Third Plenary Session and then go to the Control Yuan to submit a statement, etc.

Pengpu Villagers Blocking the Train on the Tracks (Photo by Huadong News Agency)

A Record of the Martyrdom of Gao Wenbin, Commander of the Fifth Military District of the Volunteer Army 138

Unbowed to the End, Worthy of Song and Tears

Central News Agency reports that Gao Wenbin, commander of the Fifth Military District of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army, died in Tieling. The outline of the situation was reported in the previous newspaper. Now, Jiang Xing, the deputy captain of the Northeast Volunteer Army Rescue Team, who returned to Shanghai from the front line, told reporters the details of the death of Commander Gao Wenbin, which are recorded below.

Reconnaissance and Arrest 139

Gao Wenbin's Fifth Military District was stationed near the Rebian area. In the past year, they had fought hard against the Japanese army, so the Japanese army hated them. On the 27th of last month, Commander Gao Wenbin of the district led dozens of guards to Tieling to reconnoiter the enemy's situation. Several Chinese traitors employed by the Japanese army were also reconnoitering in the area. The traitors saw Gao and immediately rushed to the Japanese army headquarters to report. After receiving the report, the Japanese army sent a battalion of infantry to the area and surrounded Gao. Gao and his guards resisted bravely, fighting for an hour, but were outnumbered and the entire army was destroyed. Gao was also captured alive.

The Circumstances of the Death 140

After Gao was captured, he was taken to the Japanese army headquarters. It is said that at that time, the Japanese army severely tortured him and forced him to confess the Volunteer Army's combat plans and defense situation. Gao refused to reveal anything and said, "My head can be broken, but my will cannot be bent." At that time, the Japanese army burned the remaining captured Volunteer Army soldiers to death in front of Gao, dousing them with kerosene. Gao witnessed the tragic scene, his eyes were torn apart, and he shouted slogans such as "Long live the Republic of China, long live the Volunteer Army," and pointed at the Japanese traitors and scolded them loudly. The Japanese army, seeing that Gao's will could not be bent, ordered him to be pushed onto the execution platform. Gao Wenbin, a loyal and brave general who had been fighting with the Japanese invaders for a year, died for his country. After hearing the news, all the soldiers of the army were heartbroken. They have now been reorganized by a certain general and will fight a desperate battle with the Japanese army to avenge Gao.

Gao's History 141

Gao Wenbin was 44 years old and from Liaoning. He was a very famous figure in the local Green Forest. After the September 18th Incident, he and his subordinates took an oath of blood and reorganized into the Volunteer Army, fighting against the Japanese army in the Tieling area. Later, the Northeast People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association in Beiping appointed Gao as the commander of the Fifth Military District of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army.

Relief Work 142

Jiang also told reporters that after the team set off, they went from Nanjing to Beiping. At that time, they stationed the team headquarters in the New World Building in Tianqiao and visited Wang Huayi, a member of the Standing Committee of the Northeast People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association. He was introduced to serve in Zheng Gui's unit and was also subsidized with 215 yuan for travel expenses. Then, I led the team to Lingnan County on the border of Guanzhong. We established a field hospital in the area and provided relief to displaced refugees. The weather outside the customs is extremely cold, and water drips become ice, and the rescue team is still wearing thin cotton clothes for battle. Food and medicine are also about to run out, so I returned to Shanghai to seek assistance from all walks of life.

Letter to the Guangdong Authorities 143

The team telegraphed the Guangdong Provincial authorities, requesting assistance with medicines, etc. The original telegram said to Chairman Chen of the Guangdong Provincial Government, all the officers and soldiers of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, Commander-in-Chief Li Denlin of Guangxi, and General Commander Bai Jiansheng: Reading the ash telegram, I am pleased to learn that the comrades are enthusiastic about the party and the country and donated counties to assist, which is a clear demonstration of righteousness. I cannot help but admire you. Since its establishment, this team has been in existence for three months. The first team has already arrived in Jinxi, undertaking the work of the Fourth Route Army under Geng Jizhou. The second team has also arrived in Ping and will leave the customs in the near future. However, repeated telegrams have been sent to urge the sending of medicines, but donations from all walks of life are few. The team's economy is also stretched and unable to purchase. Even exhausting the lake to fish is difficult to remedy. I hereby telegraphed to all comrades, urgently requesting assistance with medical supplies so that the team can receive assistance. I am extremely eager for it. Fei Jian, Wu Huiquan, and Xu Huiren of the Shanghai Office of the Northeast Volunteer Army Rescue Team, bow their heads.

Resolution of the Labor Dispute at the China Merchants Electric Tram Company 144

Both Sides Will Formally Sign the Agreement on a Set Date

The labor dispute at the China Merchants Electric Tram Company in the city, in which all workers demanded a general wage increase, was submitted to the city government for arbitration after mediation by the city's Social Affairs Bureau failed. To seek a resolution, the labor and management sides directly engaged in reconciliation, and with the strong persuasion of Mr. Du Yuesheng, it was finally determined that each worker would receive a general wage increase of three yuan starting in October of this year, as well as a principle of five days of annual bonus. The company authorities specially passed a resolution at a board meeting last Saturday and appointed three directors, Lu Bohong, Zhang Xiaoliang, and Gu Xinyi, as signing representatives. The labor union also convened a temporary representative meeting at 10:00 a.m. yesterday, attended by more than 50 responsible representatives from various departments. The meeting was chaired by Lu Jiyun, and Lu Yinchu, a cadre from the Civil Training Section of the Municipal Party Department, attended to provide guidance. After Hu Yida, the attending representative who handled the salary increase, reported the progress of the reconciliation, the discussion began. ㈠ The company has agreed that all workers in all departments will receive a general wage increase of three yuan starting in October of this year, and that the annual bonus will be increased by five days uniformly. Resolved: Passed unanimously. ㈡ It was resolved that the authorities should be requested to release Yu Jinfu, Huang Defang, Wang Hesheng, Song Rengui, and other four workers who were arrested by the Public Security Bureau during the labor dispute. Resolved: Request the Municipal Party Department to bail them out as soon as possible. ㈢ The representatives for signing the agreement were appointed. Resolved: Hu Yida, Fu Chongde, and Tan Minglin were appointed as the signing representatives. It is rumored that the formal signing will take place the day after tomorrow.
